It is expected that no new request is sent after a\n    64→  // response is received until the Envoy instance is ready to ACK/NACK the new\n    65→  // configuration. ACK/NACK takes place by returning the new API config version\n    66→  // as applied or the previous API config version respectively. Each ``type_url``\n    67→  // (see below) has an independent version associated with it.\n    68→  string version_info = 1;\n    69→\n    70→  // The node making the request.\n    71→  config.core.v3.Node node = 2;\n    72→\n    73→  // List of resources to subscribe to, e.g. list of cluster names or a route\n    74→  // configuration name. If this is empty, all resources for the API are\n    75→  // returned. LDS/CDS may have empty ``resource_names``, which will cause all\n    76→  // resources for the Envoy instance to be returned. These resources are typed and depend on the API being called.\n   124→  repeated google.protobuf.Any resources = 2;\n   125→\n   126→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   127→  // Canary is used to support two Envoy command line flags:\n   128→  //\n   129→  // * ``--terminate-on-canary-transition-failure``. When set, Envoy is able to\n   130→  //   terminate if it detects that configuration is stuck at canary. Consider\n   131→  //   this example sequence of updates:\n   132→  //\n   133→  //   * Management server applies a canary config successfully.\n   134→  //   * Management server rolls back to a production config.\n   135→  //   * Envoy rejects the new production config.\n   136→  //\n   137→  //   Since there is no sensible way to continue receiving configuration\n   138→  //   updates, Envoy will then terminate and apply production config from a\n   139→  //   clean slate.\n   140→  //\n   141→  // * ``--dry-run-canary``. When set, a canary response will never be applied, only\n   142→  //   validated via a dry run.\n   143→  //\n   144→  bool canary = 3;\n   145→\n   146→  // Type URL for resources. Identifies the xDS API when muxing over ADS.\n   147→  // Must be consistent with the ``type_url`` in the 'resources' repeated Any (if non-empty).\n   148→  string type_url = 4;\n   149→\n   150→  // For gRPC based subscriptions, the nonce provides a way to explicitly ack a\n   151→  // specific ``DiscoveryResponse`` in a following ``DiscoveryRequest``. Additional\n   152→  // messages may have been sent by Envoy to the management server for the\n   153→  // previous version on the stream prior to this ``DiscoveryResponse``, that were\n   154→  // unprocessed at response send time. The nonce allows the management server\n   155→  // to ignore any further ``DiscoveryRequests`` for the previous version until a\n   156→  // ``DiscoveryRequest`` bearing the nonce. The nonce is optional and is not\n   157→  // required for non-stream based xDS implementations.\n   158→  string nonce = 5;\n   159→\n   160→  // The control plane instance that sent the response.\n   161→  config.core.v3.ControlPlane control_plane = 6;\n   162→\n   163→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   164→  // Errors associated with specific resources. Clients are expected to\n   165→  // remember the most recent error for a given resource across responses;\n   166→  // the error condition is not considered to be cleared until a response is\n   167→  // received that contains the resource in the 'resources' field.\n   168→  repeated ResourceError resource_errors = 7;\n   169→}\n   170→\n   171→// DeltaDiscoveryRequest and DeltaDiscoveryResponse are used in a new gRPC\n   172→// endpoint for Delta xDS.\n   173→//\n   174→// With Delta xDS, the DeltaDiscoveryResponses do not need to include a full\n   175→// snapshot of the tracked resources. Instead, DeltaDiscoveryResponses are a\n   176→// diff to the state of a xDS client.\n   177→// In Delta XDS there are per-resource versions, which allow tracking state at\n   178→// the resource granularity.\n   179→// An xDS Delta session is always in the context of a gRPC bidirectional\n   180→// stream. This allows the xDS server to keep track of the state of xDS clients\n   181→// connected to it.\n   182→//\n   183→// In Delta xDS the nonce field is required and used to pair\n   184→// ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse`` to a ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` ACK or NACK.\n   185→// Optionally, a response message level ``system_version_info`` is present for\n   186→// debugging purposes only.\n   187→//\n   188→// ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` plays two independent roles. Any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``\n   189→// can be either or both of:\n   190→//\n   191→// * Informing the server of what resources the client has gained/lost interest in\n   192→//   (using ``resource_names_subscribe`` and ``resource_names_unsubscribe``), or\n   193→// * (N)ACKing an earlier resource update from the server (using ``response_nonce``,\n   194→//   with presence of ``error_detail`` making it a NACK).\n   195→//\n   196→// Additionally, the first message (for a given ``type_url``) of a reconnected gRPC stream\n   197→// has a third role: informing the server of the resources (and their versions)\n   198→// that the client already possesses, using the ``initial_resource_versions`` field.\n   199→//\n   200→// As with state-of-the-world, when multiple resource types are multiplexed (ADS),\n   201→// all requests/acknowledgments/updates are logically walled off by ``type_url``:\n   202→// a Cluster ACK exists in a completely separate world from a prior Route NACK.\n   203→// In particular, ``initial_resource_versions`` being sent at the \"start\" of every\n   204→// gRPC stream actually entails a message for each ``type_url``, each with its own\n   205→// ``initial_resource_versions``.\n   206→// [#next-free-field: 10]\n   207→message DeltaDiscoveryRequest {\n   208→  option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type = \"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryRequest\";\n   209→\n   210→  // The node making the request.\n   211→  config.core.v3.Node node = 1;\n   212→\n   213→  // Type of the resource that is being requested, e.g.\n   214→  // ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.api.v2.ClusterLoadAssignment``. This does not need to be set if\n   215→  // resources are only referenced via ``xds_resource_subscribe`` and\n   216→  // ``xds_resources_unsubscribe``.\n   217→  string type_url = 2;\n   218→\n   219→  // DeltaDiscoveryRequests allow the client to add or remove individual\n   220→  // resources to the set of tracked resources in the context of a stream.\n   221→  // All resource names in the ``resource_names_subscribe`` list are added to the\n   222→  // set of tracked resources and all resource names in the ``resource_names_unsubscribe``\n   223→  // list are removed from the set of tracked resources.\n   224→  //\n   225→  // *Unlike* state-of-the-world xDS, an empty ``resource_names_subscribe`` or\n   226→  // ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` list simply means that no resources are to be\n   227→  // added or removed to the resource list.\n   228→  // *Like* state-of-the-world xDS, the server must send updates for all tracked\n   229→  // resources, but can also send updates for resources the client has not subscribed to.\n   230→  //\n   231→  // .. note::\n   232→  //   The server must respond with all resources listed in ``resource_names_subscribe``,\n   233→  //   even if it believes the client has the most recent version of them. The reason:\n   234→  //   the client may have dropped them, but then regained interest before it had a chance\n   235→  //   to send the unsubscribe message. See DeltaSubscriptionStateTest.RemoveThenAdd.\n   236→  //\n   237→  // These two fields can be set in any ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest``, including ACKs\n   238→  // and ``initial_resource_versions``.\n   239→  //\n   240→  // A list of Resource names to add to the list of tracked resources.\n   241→  repeated string resource_names_subscribe = 3;\n   242→\n   243→  // A list of Resource names to remove from the list of tracked resources.\n   244→  repeated string resource_names_unsubscribe = 4;\n   245→\n   246→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   247→  // Alternative to ``resource_names_subscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\n   248→  // along with each resource name.\n   249→  //\n   250→  // .. note::\n   251→  //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\n   252→  //   in ``resource_names_subscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_subscribe``.\n   253→  //\n   254→  repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_subscribe = 8;\n   255→\n   256→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   257→  // Alternative to ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` field that allows specifying dynamic parameters\n   258→  // along with each resource name.\n   259→  //\n   260→  // .. note::\n   261→  //   It is legal for a request to have some resources listed\n   262→  //   in ``resource_names_unsubscribe`` and others in ``resource_locators_unsubscribe``.\n   263→  //\n   264→  repeated ResourceLocator resource_locators_unsubscribe = 9;\n   265→\n   266→  // Informs the server of the versions of the resources the xDS client knows of, to enable the\n   267→  // client to continue the same logical xDS session even in the face of gRPC stream reconnection.\n   268→  // It will not be populated:\n   269→  //\n   270→  // * In the very first stream of a session, since the client will not yet have any resources.\n   271→  // * In any message after the first in a stream (for a given ``type_url``), since the server will\n   272→  //   already be correctly tracking the client's state.\n   273→  //\n   274→  // (In ADS, the first message ``of each type_url`` of a reconnected stream populates this map.)\n   275→  // The map's keys are names of xDS resources known to the xDS client.\n   276→  // The map's values are opaque resource versions.\n   277→  map<string, string> initial_resource_versions = 5;\n   278→\n   279→  // When the ``DeltaDiscoveryRequest`` is a ACK or NACK message in response\n   280→  // to a previous ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse``, the ``response_nonce`` must be the\n   281→  // nonce in the ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse``.\n   282→  // Otherwise (unlike in ``DiscoveryRequest``) ``response_nonce`` must be omitted.\n   283→  string response_nonce = 6;\n   284→\n   285→  // This is populated when the previous :ref:`DiscoveryResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.discovery.v3.DiscoveryResponse>`\n   286→  // failed to update configuration. The ``message`` field in ``error_details``\n   287→  // provides the Envoy internal exception related to the failure.\n   288→  google.rpc.Status error_detail = 7;\n   289→}\n   290→\n   291→// [#next-free-field: 10]\n   292→message DeltaDiscoveryResponse {\n   293→  option (udpa.annotations.versioning).previous_message_type =\n   294→      \"envoy.api.v2.DeltaDiscoveryResponse\";\n   295→\n   296→  // The version of the response data (used for debugging).\n   297→  string system_version_info = 1;\n   298→\n   299→  // The response resources. These are typed resources, whose types must match\n   300→  // the ``type_url`` field.\n   301→  repeated Resource resources = 2;\n   302→\n   303→  // field id 3 IS available!\n   304→\n   305→  // Type URL for resources. Identifies the xDS API when muxing over ADS.\n   306→  // Must be consistent with the ``type_url`` in the Any within 'resources' if 'resources' is non-empty.\n   307→  string type_url = 4;\n   308→\n   309→  // Resource names of resources that have been deleted and to be removed from the xDS Client.\n   310→  // Removed resources for missing resources can be ignored.\n   311→  repeated string removed_resources = 6;\n   312→\n   313→  // Alternative to ``removed_resources`` that allows specifying which variant of\n   314→  // a resource is being removed. This variant must be used for any resource\n   315→  // for which dynamic parameter constraints were sent to the client.\n   316→  repeated ResourceName removed_resource_names = 8;\n   317→\n   318→  // The nonce provides a way for ``DeltaDiscoveryRequests`` to uniquely\n   319→  // reference a ``DeltaDiscoveryResponse`` when (N)ACKing. The nonce is required.\n   320→  string nonce = 5;\n   321→\n   322→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   323→  // The control plane instance that sent the response.\n   324→  config.core.v3.ControlPlane control_plane = 7;\n   325→\n   326→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   327→  // Errors associated with specific resources.\n   328→  //\n   329→  // .. note::\n   330→  //   A resource in this field with a status of NOT_FOUND should be treated the same as\n   331→  //   a resource listed in the ``removed_resources`` or ``removed_resource_names`` fields.\n   332→  //\n   333→  repeated ResourceError resource_errors = 9;\n   334→}\n   335→\n   336→// A set of dynamic parameter constraints associated with a variant of an individual xDS resource.\n   337→// These constraints determine whether the resource matches a subscription based on the set of\n   338→// dynamic parameters in the subscription, as specified in the\n   339→// :ref:`ResourceLocator.dynamic_parameters <envoy_v3_api_field_service.discovery.v3.ResourceLocator.dynamic_parameters>`\n   340→// field. against.\n   349→    string key = 1;\n   350→\n   351→    oneof constraint_type {\n   352→      option (validate.required) = true;\n   353→\n   354→      // Matches this exact value.\n   355→      string value = 2;\n   356→\n   357→      // Key is present (matches any value except for the key being absent).\n   358→      // This allows setting a default constraint for clients that do\n   359→      // not send a key at all, while there may be other clients that need\n   360→      // special configuration based on that key.\n   361→      Exists exists = 3;\n   362→    }\n   363→  }\n   364→\n 376→\n   377→    // A list of constraints that must all match.\n   378→    ConstraintList and_constraints = 3;\n   379→\n   380→    // The inverse (NOT) of a set of constraints.\n   381→    DynamicParameterConstraints not_constraints = 4;\n   382→  }\n   383→}\n   384→\n   385→// [#next-free-field: 10]\n   386→message Resource {\n   387→  option aliases = 4;\n   413→\n   414→  // The resource level version. It allows xDS to track the state of individual\n   415→  // resources.\n   416→  string version = 1;\n   417→\n   418→  // The resource being tracked.\n   419→  google.protobuf.Any resource = 2;\n   420→\n   421→  // Time-to-live value for the resource. For each resource, a timer is started. The timer is\n   422→  // reset each time the resource is received with a new TTL. If the resource is received with\n   423→  // no TTL set, the timer is removed for the resource. Upon expiration of the timer, the\n   424→  // configuration for the resource will be removed.\n   425→  //\n   426→  // The TTL can be refreshed or changed by sending a response that doesn't change the resource\n   427→  // version. In this case the ``resource`` field does not need to be populated, which allows for\n   428→  // light-weight \"heartbeat\" updates to keep a resource with a TTL alive.\n   429→  //\n   430→  // The TTL feature is meant to support configurations that should be removed in the event of\n   431→  // a management server failure. For example, the feature may be used for fault injection\n   432→  // testing where the fault injection should be terminated in the event that Envoy loses contact\n   433→  // with the management server.\n   434→  google.protobuf.Duration ttl = 6;\n   435→\n   436→  // Cache control properties for the resource.\n   437→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   438→  CacheControl cache_control = 7;\n   439→\n   440→  // The Metadata field can be used to provide additional information for the resource.\n   441→  // E.g. the trace data for debugging.\n   442→  config.core.v3.Metadata metadata = 9;\n   443→}\n   444→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. logical xDS session even in the face of gRPC stream reconnection.\n  // It will not be populated:\n  //\n  // * In the very first stream of a session, since the client will not yet have any resources.\n  // * In any message after the first in a stream (for a given ``type_url``), since the server will\n  //   already be correctly tracking the client's state.\n  //\n  // (In ADS, the first This allows xDS implementations (clients, servers, and caching proxies) to determine\n// which variant of a resource is appropriate for a given client.\nmessage DynamicParameterConstraints {\n  // A single constraint for a given key.\n  message SingleConstraint {\n    message Exists {\n    }\n\n    // The key to match against.\n    string key = 1;\n\n    oneof constraint_type {\n      option }\n  }\n\n  message ConstraintList {\n    repeated DynamicParameterConstraints constraints = 1;\n  }\n\n  oneof type {\n    // A single constraint to evaluate.\n    SingleConstraint constraint = 1;\n\n    // A list of constraints that match if any one constraint in the list\n    // matches.\n    ConstraintList or_constraints = 2;\n\n    // A list of constraints that must all match.\n    ConstraintList and_constraints = 3;\n\n    // The inverse (NOT) of a set of constraints.\n    DynamicParameterConstraints not_constraints = 4;\n  }\n}\n\n// [#next-free-field: 10]\nmessage Resource own use, regardless of the value of this field.\n    //\n    bool do_not_cache = 1;\n  }\n\n  // The resource's name, to distinguish it from others of the same type of resource.\n  // Only one of ``name`` or ``resource_name`` may be set.\n  string name = 3;\n\n  // Alternative to the ``name`` field, to be used when the server supports\n  // multiple variants of the named resource that are differentiated by\n  // dynamic parameter constraints.\n  // Only one of ``name`` or ``resource_name`` may be set.\n  ResourceName resource_name = 8;\n\n  // The aliases are a list of other names that It allows xDS to track the state of individual\n  // resources.\n  string version = 1;\n\n  // The resource being tracked.\n  google.protobuf.Any resource = 2;\n\n  // Time-to-live value for the resource. For each resource, a timer is started. The timer is\n  // reset each time the resource is received with a new TTL. If the resource is received with\n  // no TTL set, the timer is removed for the resource. Upon expiration of the timer, the\n  // configuration for the resource will be removed.\n  //\n  // The TTL can be refreshed or changed by sending a response that doesn't change the resource\n  // version. In this case the ``resource`` field does not need to be populated, which allows for\n  // light-weight \"heartbeat\" updates to keep a resource with a TTL alive.\n  //\n  // The TTL feature is meant to support configurations that should be removed in the event of\n  // a management server failure. They will always all be blissfully\n// unaware of each other's existence, even when their messages are being multiplexed together by\n// ADS.\n//\n// There are two scenarios which affect how DeltaSubscriptionState manages the resources. First\n// scenario is when we are subscribed to a wildcard resource, and other scenario is when we are not.\n//\n// Delta subscription state also divides the resources it cached into three categories: requested,\n// wildcard and ambiguous.\n//\n// The \"requested\" category is for resources that we have explicitly asked for (either through the\n// initial set of resources or through the on-demand mechanism). Resources in this category are in\n// one of two states: \"complete\" and \"waiting for server\".\n//\n// \"Complete\" resources are resources about which the server sent us the information we need (for\n// now - just resource version).\n//\n// The \"waiting for server\" state is either for resources that we have just requested, but we still\n// didn't receive any version information from the server, or for the \"complete\" resources that,\n// according to the server, are gone, but we are still interested in them - in such case we strip\n// the information from the resource.\n//\n// The \"wildcard\" category is for resources that we are not explicitly interested in, but we are\n// indirectly interested through the subscription to the wildcard resource.\n//\n// The \"ambiguous\" category is for resources that we stopped being interested in, but we may still\n// be interested indirectly through the wildcard subscription. So when we unsubscribe from the resource, we need to\n// receive a confirmation from the server whether to keep the resource (which means that it was a\n// part of our wildcard subscription) or to drop it.\n//\n// Please refer to drawings (non-wildcard-resource-state-machine.png and\n// (wildcard-resource-state-machine.png) for visual depictions of the resource state machine.\n//\n// In the \"no wildcard subscription\" scenario all the cached resources should be in the \"requested\"\n// category. Resources are added to the category upon the explicit request and dropped when we\n// explicitly unsubscribe from it. Transitions between \"complete\" and \"waiting for server\" happen\n// when we receive messages from the server - if a resource in the message is in \"added resources\"\n// list (thus contains version information), the resource becomes \"complete\". If the resource in the\n// message is in \"removed resources\" list, it changes into the \"waiting for server\" state. If a\n// server sends us a resource that we didn't request, it's going to be ignored.\n//\n// In the \"wildcard subscription\" scenario, \"requested\" category is the same as in \"no wildcard\n// subscription\" scenario, with one exception - the unsubscribed \"complete\" resource is not removed\n// from the cache, but it's moved to the \"ambiguous\" resources instead. At this point we are waiting\n// for the server to tell us that this resource should be either moved to the \"wildcard\" resources,\n// or dropped. Resources in \"wildcard\" category are only added there or dropped from there by the\n// server. Resources from both \"wildcard\" and \"ambiguous\" categories can become \"requested\"\n// \"complete\" resources if we subscribe to them again.\n//\n// The delta subscription state transitions between the two scenarios depending on whether we are\n// subscribed to wildcard resource or not. configuration discovery service flow follows a chain from the data plane API definition through the control plane Go implementation to the Envoy C++ client:\\n\\n**Protocol Definition (envoyproxy/data-plane-api):**\\nThe `envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads.proto` file defines the `AggregatedDiscoveryService` gRPC service with two primary RPCs:\\n- `StreamAggregatedResources(stream DiscoveryRequest) returns (stream DiscoveryResponse)` - State-of-the-world (SOTW) xDS\\n- `DeltaAggregatedResources(stream DeltaDiscoveryRequest) returns (stream DeltaDiscoveryResponse)` - Delta xDS\\n\\nThe message types (`DiscoveryRequest`, `DiscoveryResponse`, `DeltaDiscoveryRequest`, `DeltaDiscoveryResponse`) are defined in `envoy/service/discovery/v3/discovery.proto`.\\n\\n**Go Control Plane (envoyproxy/go-control-plane):**\\nThe protoc-gen-go-grpc compiler generates gRPC stubs in `envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads_grpc.pb.go` with the `AggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer` interface and handlers for `StreamAggregatedResources` and `DeltaAggregatedResources`. The Go bindings for `DiscoveryRequest` and `DiscoveryResponse` message types are in `envoy/service/discovery/v3/discovery.pb.go`.\\n\\n**Envoy Client (envoyproxy/envoy):**\\nThe configuration subscription flow in Envoy implements a layered architecture:\\n\\n1. **Subscription Layer** (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_subscription_impl.h`): `GrpcSubscriptionImpl` provides a typed subscription adapter that wraps the untyped `GrpcMux` and handles per-xDS API stats and callbacks.\\n\\n2. **Mux Layer** (`envoy/config/grpc_mux.h`): The `GrpcMux` interface manages one or more gRPC subscriptions on a single stream to the management server. Two implementations exist:\\n   - `GrpcMuxImpl` (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_impl.h`): Handles state-of-the-world (SOTW) xDS using `DiscoveryRequest`/`DiscoveryResponse`\\n   - `NewGrpcMuxImpl` (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/new_grpc_mux_impl.h`): Handles Delta xDS using `DeltaDiscoveryRequest`/`DeltaDiscoveryResponse`\\n\\n3. **Stream Layer** (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_stream_interface.h`): The `GrpcStreamInterface` template defines the abstract interface for gRPC communication.\\n\\n4. **Stream Implementation** (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_stream.h`): The `GrpcStream` template class implements the actual bidirectional gRPC streaming using gRPC's `AsyncStreamCallbacks`. It:\\n   - Establishes the gRPC channel using `establishNewStream()`\\n   - Sends `DiscoveryRequest` or `DeltaDiscoveryRequest` messages via `sendMessage()`\\n   - Receives responses in `onReceiveMessage()` and invokes `callbacks_->onDiscoveryResponse()` with the response\\n   - Handles rate limiting and connection management\\n\\n5. **Delta State Management** (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/delta_subscription_state.h`): For Delta xDS, `DeltaSubscriptionState` maintains the protocol state, managing resource subscription interest and generating appropriate `DeltaDiscoveryRequest` messages in response to `DeltaDiscoveryResponse` messages.\\n\\n**Configuration Update Flow:**\\nWhen an Envoy client needs configuration (e.g., clusters, routes, endpoints):\\n1. A resource subscriber calls `GrpcSubscriptionImpl::start()` with resource names\\n2. This calls `GrpcMux::addWatch()` to register interest\\n3. configuration discovery service flow follows a chain from the data plane API definition through the control plane Go implementation to the Envoy C++ client:\\n\\n**Protocol Definition (envoyproxy/data-plane-api):**\\nThe `envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads.proto` file defines the `AggregatedDiscoveryService` gRPC service with two primary RPCs:\\n- `StreamAggregatedResources(stream DiscoveryRequest) returns (stream DiscoveryResponse)` - State-of-the-world (SOTW) xDS\\n- `DeltaAggregatedResources(stream DeltaDiscoveryRequest) returns (stream DeltaDiscoveryResponse)` - Delta xDS\\n\\nThe message types (`DiscoveryRequest`, `DiscoveryResponse`, `DeltaDiscoveryRequest`, `DeltaDiscoveryResponse`) are defined in `envoy/service/discovery/v3/discovery.proto`.\\n\\n**Go Control Plane (envoyproxy/go-control-plane):**\\nThe protoc-gen-go-grpc compiler generates gRPC stubs in `envoy/service/discovery/v3/ads_grpc.pb.go` with the `AggregatedDiscoveryServiceServer` interface and handlers for `StreamAggregatedResources` and `DeltaAggregatedResources`. The Go bindings for `DiscoveryRequest` and `DiscoveryResponse` message types are in `envoy/service/discovery/v3/discovery.pb.go`.\\n\\n**Envoy Client (envoyproxy/envoy):**\\nThe configuration subscription flow in Envoy implements a layered architecture:\\n\\n1. **Subscription Layer** (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_subscription_impl.h`): `GrpcSubscriptionImpl` provides a typed subscription adapter that wraps the untyped `GrpcMux` and handles per-xDS API stats and callbacks.\\n\\n2. **Mux Layer** (`envoy/config/grpc_mux.h`): The `GrpcMux` interface manages one or more gRPC subscriptions on a single stream to the management server. Two implementations exist:\\n   - `GrpcMuxImpl` (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_mux_impl.h`): Handles state-of-the-world (SOTW) xDS using `DiscoveryRequest`/`DiscoveryResponse`\\n   - `NewGrpcMuxImpl` (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/new_grpc_mux_impl.h`): Handles Delta xDS using `DeltaDiscoveryRequest`/`DeltaDiscoveryResponse`\\n\\n3. **Stream Layer** (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_stream_interface.h`): The `GrpcStreamInterface` template defines the abstract interface for gRPC communication.\\n\\n4. **Stream Implementation** (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/grpc_stream.h`): The `GrpcStream` template class implements the actual bidirectional gRPC streaming using gRPC's `AsyncStreamCallbacks`. It:\\n   - Establishes the gRPC channel using `establishNewStream()`\\n   - Sends `DiscoveryRequest` or `DeltaDiscoveryRequest` messages via `sendMessage()`\\n   - Receives responses in `onReceiveMessage()` and invokes `callbacks_->onDiscoveryResponse()` with the response\\n   - Handles rate limiting and connection management\\n\\n5. **Delta State Management** (`source/extensions/config_subscription/grpc/delta_subscription_state.h`): For Delta xDS, `DeltaSubscriptionState` maintains the protocol state, managing resource subscription interest and generating appropriate `DeltaDiscoveryRequest` messages in response to `DeltaDiscoveryResponse` messages.\\n\\n**Configuration Update Flow:**\\nWhen an Envoy client needs configuration (e.g., clusters, routes, endpoints):\\n1. A resource subscriber calls `GrpcSubscriptionImpl::start()` with resource names\\n2. This calls `GrpcMux::addWatch()` to register interest\\n3.
